presidential election in Rhode Island, 2000" /></map><img alt="ElectoralCollege2000.svg" </td> </tr> <tr> <td colspan="4"> <hr /> <table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="background:transparent; width:100%;"> <tr> <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; text-size: 80%"><b>President before election</b><br /> <p><a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a><br /> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a></p> </td> <td style="width:50%; text-align:right; text-size: 80%"><b>Elected President</b><br /> <p><a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a><br /> <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a></p> </td> </tr> </table> </td> </tr> </table> <p>The <b>United States presidential election of 2000</b> was the 54th quadrennial <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">presidential election</a>. It was held on Tuesday, November 7, 2000. The contest was between <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">governor of Texas</a> and son of former president <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a>.</p> <p>Incumbent Democratic <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> was not eligible to serve a third term, and Vice President Gore was able to secure the Democratic nomination with relative ease. Bush was seen as the early favorite for the Republican nomination, and despite a contentious primary battle with Senator <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> and other candidates, secured the nomination by <a href="/wiki/Super_Tuesday" title="Super Tuesday">Super Tuesday</a>. Many third party candidates also ran, most prominently <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">Ralph Nader</a>. Bush chose former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">Secretary of Defense</a> Dick Cheney as his running mate, and Gore chose Senator <a href="/wiki/Joe_Lieberman" title="Joe Lieberman">Joe Lieberman</a> as his. Both major party candidates focused primarily on domestic issues, such as the budget, tax relief, and reforms for federal <a href="/wiki/Social_insurance" title="Social insurance">social insurance</a> programs, though foreign policy was not ignored. Clinton and Gore did not often campaign together, a deliberate decision resulting from the <a href="/wiki/Lewinsky_scandal" title="Lewinsky scandal">Lewinsky sex scandal</a> two years prior.</p> <p>Election results hinged on <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Florida,_2000" title="United States presidential election in Florida, 2000">Florida</a>, where the margin of victory triggered a mandatory recount. Litigation in select counties started additional recounts, and this litigation ultimately reached the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">United States Supreme Court</a>. The Court's contentious decision in <i><a href="/wiki/Bush_v._Gore" title="Bush v. Gore">Bush v. Gore</a></i> (in contrast to an equally contentious decision by the Florida State Supreme Court), announced on December 12, 2000, ended the recounts, effectively awarding Florida's votes to Bush and granting him the victory. This marked the fourth election in U.S. history in which the eventual winner failed to win a plurality of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_vote" title="Popular vote" class="mw-redirect">popular vote</a> (after the elections of <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1824" title="United States presidential election, 1824">1824</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1876" title="United States presidential election, 1876">1876</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1888" title="United States presidential election, 1888">1888</a>). Later studies have <a href="#Aftermath">reached conflicting opinions</a> on who would have won the recount had it been allowed to proceed.</p> <p></p> <div id="toc" class="toc"> <div id="toctitle"> nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Democratic Party nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries,_2000" title="Democratic Party presidential primaries, 2000">Democratic Party presidential primaries, 2000</a></div> <p>Democratic candidates</p> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, Vice President of the United States from <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a></li> <li><a href="/wiki/Bill_Bradley" title="Bill Bradley">Bill Bradley</a>, former U.S. Senator from <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> (withdrew on March 9, 2000 and endorsed Al Gore)</li> </ul> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Candidates_gallery">Candidates gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Candidates gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 652px;_width: 652px;"> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Al_Gore,_Vice_President_of_the_United_States,_official_portrait_1994.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Al_Gore%2C_Vice_President_of_the_United_States%2C_official_portrait_1994.jpg/96px-Al_Gore%2C_Vice_President_of_the_United_States%2C_official_portrait_1994.jpg" width="96" height="120" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p><a href="/wiki/U.S._Vice_President" title="U.S. Vice President" class="mw-redirect">Vice President</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> (<a href="/wiki/Al_Gore_presidential_campaign,_2000" title="Al Gore presidential campaign, 2000">campaign</a>)</p> </div> </div> </li> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Senator_Bill_Bradley_(D-NJ).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Senator_Bill_Bradley_%28D-NJ%29.jpg/102px-Senator_Bill_Bradley_%28D-NJ%29.jpg" width="102" height="120" data-file-width="191" data-file-height="225" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p>Former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Bill_Bradley" title="Bill Bradley">Bill Bradley</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> (Withdrew on March 9, 2000)</p> </div> </div> </li> </ul> <p><a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> was a consistent front-runner for the nomination. Other prominent Democrats mentioned as possible contenders included <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kerrey" title="Bob Kerrey">Bob Kerrey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> Congressman <a href="/wiki/Dick_Gephardt" title="Dick Gephardt">Dick Gephardt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a> Senator <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wellstone" title="Paul Wellstone">Paul Wellstone</a>, and famous actor and director <a href="/wiki/Warren_Beatty" title="Warren Beatty">Warren Beatty</a>, who declined to run.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Of these, only Wellstone formed an <a href="/wiki/Exploratory_committee" title="Exploratory committee">exploratory committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>In addition to Gore's advantage as the incumbent Vice President, Bradley was not the candidate of a major faction or coalition of blocs. Running an insurgency campaign, Bradley positioned himself as the alternative to Gore, who was a founding member of the centrist <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Leadership_Council" title="Democratic Leadership Council">Democratic Leadership Council</a>. While former basketball star <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a> campaigned for him in the early primary states, Bradley announced his intention to campaign "in a different way" by conducting a positive campaign of "big ideas". The focus of his campaign was a plan to spend the record-breaking budget surplus on a variety of social welfare programs to help the poor and the middle-class, along with campaign finance reform and <a href="/wiki/Gun_control" title="Gun control">gun control</a>.</p> <p>Gore easily defeated Bradley in the primaries, largely because of support from the Democratic Party establishment and Bradley's poor showing in the Iowa caucus, where Gore successfully painted Bradley as aloof and indifferent to the plight of farmers. The closest Bradley came to a victory was his 50–46 loss to Gore in the New Hampshire primary. On March 14, Al Gore won the Democratic nomination.</p> <p>None of Bradley's delegates were allowed to vote for him, so Gore won the nomination unanimously at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2000 Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a>. <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> Senator <a href="/wiki/Joe_Lieberman" title="Joe Lieberman">Joe Lieberman</a> was nominated for Vice President by voice vote. Lieberman became the first <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">Jewish American</a> ever to be chosen for this position by a major party. Gore chose Lieberman over five finalists.<sup id="cite_ref-GoreLiebermanCNN_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoreLiebermanCNN-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>Delegate totals:</p> <ul> <li>Vice President Albert Gore Jr. 4328</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Abstentions" title="Abstentions" class="mw-redirect">Abstentions</a> 9</li> </ul> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_Party_nomination">Republican Party nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Republican Party nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_2000" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 2000">Republican Party presidential primaries, 2000</a></div> <dl> <dt>Republican candidates</dt> </dl> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Governor</a> of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a></li> <li><a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> from <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> (withdrew on March 9, 2000 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Alan_Keyes" title="Alan Keyes">Alan Keyes</a>, former U.S. <a href="/wiki/ECOSOC" title="ECOSOC" class="mw-redirect">ECOSOC</a> Ambassador from <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> (withdrew on July 25, 2000 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Steve_Forbes" title="Steve Forbes">Steve Forbes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Businessperson" title="Businessperson">businessman</a> from New Jersey (withdrew on February 10, 2000 and endorsed John McCain. He then endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Bauer" title="Gary Bauer">Gary Bauer</a>, former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Education" title="United States Secretary of Education">Undersecretary of Education</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> (withdrew on February 4, 2000 and endorsed John McCain. He then endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Orrin_Hatch" title="Orrin Hatch">Orrin Hatch</a>, Senator from <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> (withdrew on January 26, 2000 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Dole" title="Elizabeth Dole">Elizabeth Dole</a>, former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Labor" title="United States Secretary of Labor">Secretary of Labor</a> from <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> (withdrew on October 20, 1999 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Pat_Buchanan" title="Pat Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>, publisher and author from <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> (withdrew on October 25, 1999 to run for the Reform Party nomination)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Dan_Quayle" title="Dan Quayle">Dan Quayle</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> from <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a> (withdrew on September 27, 1999 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Lamar_Alexander" title="Lamar Alexander">Lamar Alexander</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Tennessee" title="Governor of Tennessee">Governor</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> (withdrew on August 22, 1999 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Smith_(American_politician)" title="Bob Smith (American politician)">Bob Smith</a>, Senator from <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> (withdrew in October 1999 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/John_Kasich" title="John Kasich">John Kasich</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">Representative</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> (withdrew in July 1999 and endorsed George W. Bush)</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Herman_Cain" title="Herman Cain">Herman Cain</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Godfather%27s_Pizza" title="Godfather's Pizza">Godfather's Pizza</a> from <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> (withdrew and endorsed Steve Forbes. He then endorsed George W. Bush)</li> </ul> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Candidates_gallery_2">Candidates gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Candidates gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 1141px;_width: 1141px;"> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:GeorgeWBush.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/GeorgeWBush.jpg/96px-GeorgeWBush.jpg" width="96" height="120" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p><a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Governor</a> <b><a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. data-file-width="291" data-file-height="356" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p>Former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Tennessee" title="Governor of Tennessee">Governor</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Lamar_Alexander" title="Lamar Alexander">Lamar Alexander</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> (Withdrew on August 22, 1999)</p> </div> </div> </li> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_C_Smith.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Robert_C_Smith.jpg/94px-Robert_C_Smith.jpg" width="94" height="120" data-file-width="177" data-file-height="225" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p>Senator <b><a href="/wiki/Bob_Smith_(American_politician)" title="Bob Smith (American politician)">Bob Smith</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> (Withdrew in October 1999)</p> </div> </div> </li> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Kasich.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/John_Kasich.jpg/98px-John_Kasich.jpg" width="98" height="120" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="526" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p><a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">Representative</a> <b><a href="/wiki/John_Kasich" title="John Kasich">John Kasich</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> (Withdrew in July 1999)</p> </div> </div> </li> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Herman_Cain_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Herman_Cain_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg/98px-Herman_Cain_by_Gage_Skidmore_4.jpg" width="98" height="120" data-file-width="2544" data-file-height="3108" /></a></div> </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p>Businessman <b><a href="/wiki/Herman_Cain" title="Herman Cain">Herman Cain</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a> (Withdrew early in campaign)</p> </div> </div> </li> </ul> <p>Several Republican candidates appeared on the national scene to challenge Gore's candidacy.</p> <p>George W. Bush became the early front-runner, acquiring unprecedented funding and a broad base of leadership support based on his governorship of Texas and the name recognition and connections of the Bush family. Former cabinet member <a href="/wiki/George_Shultz" title="George Shultz" class="mw-redirect">George Shultz</a> played an important early role in securing establishment Republican support for Bush. In April 1998, he invited Bush to discuss policy issues with experts including <a href="/wiki/Michael_Boskin" title="Michael Boskin">Michael Boskin</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_B._Taylor" title="John B. Taylor">John Taylor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a>. The group, which was "looking for a candidate for 2000 with good political instincts, someone they could work with", was impressed, and Shultz encouraged him to enter the race.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Several aspirants withdrew before the <a href="/wiki/Iowa_Republican_caucuses,_2000" title="Iowa Republican caucuses, 2000">Iowa Caucus</a> because they were unable to secure funding and endorsements sufficient to remain competitive with Bush. These included <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Dole" title="Elizabeth Dole">Elizabeth Dole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Quayle" title="Dan Quayle">Dan Quayle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Alexander" title="Lamar Alexander">Lamar Alexander</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Smith_(American_politician)" title="Bob Smith (American politician)">Bob Smith</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pat_Buchanan" title="Pat Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a> dropped out to run for the Reform Party nomination. That left Bush, <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Keyes" title="Alan Keyes">Alan Keyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Forbes" title="Steve Forbes">Steve Forbes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Bauer" title="Gary Bauer">Gary Bauer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orrin_Hatch" title="Orrin Hatch">Orrin Hatch</a> as the only candidates still in the race.</p> <p>On January 24, Bush won the Iowa caucus with 41% of the vote. Forbes came in second with 30% of the vote. Keyes received 14%, Bauer 9%, McCain 5%, and Hatch 1%. Hatch dropped out. On the national stage, Bush was portrayed in the media as the establishment candidate. McCain, with the support of many moderate Republicans and Independents, portrayed himself as a crusading insurgent who focused on <a href="/wiki/Electoral_reform" title="Electoral reform">campaign reform</a>.</p> <p>On February 1, McCain won a 49–30% victory over Bush in the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Presidential_primary" title="New Hampshire Presidential primary" class="mw-redirect">New Hampshire primary</a>. Gary Bauer dropped out. After coming in third in Delaware Forbes dropped out, leaving three candidates. In the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Republican_primary,_2000" title="South Carolina Republican primary, 2000" class="mw-redirect">South Carolina primary</a>, Bush soundly defeated McCain. Some McCain supporters blamed it on the Bush campaign, accusing them of mudslinging and dirty tricks, such as <a href="/wiki/Push_poll" title="Push poll">push polling</a> that implied that McCain's adopted Bangladeshi-born daughter was an African-American child he fathered out of wedlock.<sup id="cite_ref-pushpolling_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pushpolling-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> While McCain's loss in South Carolina damaged his campaign, he won both Michigan and his home state of Arizona on February 22.</p> <p>On February 24, McCain criticized Bush for accepting the endorsement of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Jones_University" title="Bob Jones University">Bob Jones University</a> despite its policy banning interracial dating. On February 28, McCain also referred to Rev. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Falwell" title="Jerry Falwell">Jerry Falwell</a> and televangelist <a href="/wiki/Pat_Robertson" title="Pat Robertson">Pat Robertson</a> as "agents of intolerance", a term he would later distance himself from during his <a href="/wiki/John_McCain_presidential_campaign,_2008" title="John McCain presidential campaign, 2008">2008 bid</a> for the party's nomination. He lost the state of Virginia to Bush on February 29. On <a href="/wiki/Super_Tuesday" title="Super Tuesday">Super Tuesday</a>, March 7, Bush won New York, Ohio, Georgia, Missouri, California, Maryland, and Maine. McCain won Rhode Island, Vermont, Connecticut, and Massachusetts, but dropped out of the race. On March 10, Alan Keyes got 21% of the vote in Utah. Bush took the majority of the remaining contests and won the Republican nomination on March 14, winning his home state of Texas and his brother <a href="/wiki/Jeb_Bush" title="Jeb Bush">Jeb's</a> home state of Florida among others. At the Republican National Convention in Philadelphia George W. Bush accepted the nomination of the Republican party.</p> <dl> <dt>Delegate totals</dt> </dl> <ul> <li>Governor George W. Bush 1526</li> <li>Senator John McCain 275</li> <li>Ambassador Dr. Alan Keyes 23</li> <li>Businessman Steve Forbes 10</li> <li>Gary Bauer 2</li> <li>None of the Names Shown 2</li> <li>Uncommitted 1</li> </ul> <p>Bush asked former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">Secretary of Defense</a> <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> to head up a team to help select a running mate for him, but ultimately, Bush decided that Cheney himself should be the vice presidential nominee. While the U.S. Constitution does not specifically disallow a president and a vice president from the same state, it does prohibit electors from casting both of his or her votes for persons from his or her own state. Accordingly, Cheney—who had been a resident of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> for nearly 10 years—changed his voting registration back to Wyoming. Had Cheney not done this, either he or Bush would have forfeited their electoral votes from the Texas electors.</p> <dl> <dt>Other mentioned candidates</dt> </dl> <ul> <li>Former Sen. <a href="/wiki/John_Danforth" title="John Danforth">John Danforth</a> of Missouri<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonMonthly_10-0" class="reference"><a Frist">Bill Frist</a> of Tennessee<sup id="cite_ref-cnn-03-05-10_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-03-05-10-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></li> <li>Sen. <a id="cite_ref-WashingtonMonthly_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonMonthly-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></li> </ul> <h3><span class="mw-headline" nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reform_Party_nomination">Reform Party nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reform Party nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_presidential_primaries,_2000" title="Reform Party presidential primaries, 2000">Reform Party presidential primaries, 2000</a></div> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_of_the_United_States_of_America" title="Reform Party of the United States of America">Reform Party</a> candidates <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/John_B._Anderson" title="John B. Anderson">John B. Anderson</a> of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, former U.S. Representative for the 16th Congressional District of <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, former Independent Presidential candidate</li> <li><a href="/wiki/David_L._Boren" title="David L. Boren">David L. Boren</a> of <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, former U.S. Senator</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Pat_Buchanan" title="Pat Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, former speechwriter and Senior Advisor to President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a></li> <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_E._Collins" title="Charles E. Collins">Charles E. Collins</a> of Georgia, former school board chairman from <a href="/wiki/Bay_County,_Florida" title="Bay County, Florida">Bay County, Florida</a></li> <li><a href="/wiki/John_Hagelin" title="John Hagelin">John Hagelin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>, Ph.D., past and then-current <a href="/wiki/Natural_Law_Party" title="Natural Law Party">Natural Law Party</a> candidate</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a> of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, 1996 presidential nominee</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, left the Republican party due to conflicting ideas on key issues</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p>The nomination went to Pat Buchanan<sup id="cite_ref-indy_weekly_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indy_weekly-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and running mate <a href="/wiki/Ezola_Foster" title="Ezola Foster" class="mw-redirect">Ezola Foster</a> of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, over the objections of party founder <a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a> and despite a rump convention nomination of <a href="/wiki/John_Hagelin" title="John Hagelin">John Hagelin</a> by the Perot faction (see Other nominations below). In the end, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Election_Commission" title="Federal Election Commission">Federal Election Commission</a> sided with Buchanan, and that ticket appeared on 49 of 51 possible ballots.</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_of_State_Green_Parties_nomination">Association of State Green Parties nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Association of State Green Parties nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <div class="thumb tright"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nader_at_O17.jpg" Kovel</a> of New York—3</li> <li>Abstain—1</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p>The <a href="/wiki/Greens/Green_Party_USA" title="Greens/Green Party USA">Greens/Green Party USA</a>, the then-recognized national party organization, later endorsed Ralph Nader for president and he appeared on the ballots of 43 states and <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia" class="mw-redirect">DC</a>.</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libertarian_Party_nomination">Libertarian Party nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Libertarian Party nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 815px;_width: 815px;"> <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"> <div style="width: 155px"> <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"> <div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarryBrowneLPCon1998.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" </div> <div class="gallerytext"> <p>Writer <b><a href="/wiki/Harry_Browne" title="Harry Browne">Harry Browne</a></b> of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a></p> </div> </div> </li> </ul> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_(United_States)" title="Libertarian Party (United States)">Libertarian Party</a> candidates delegate totals:<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Browne" title="Harry Browne">Harry Browne</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>—493</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Don_Gorman" title="Don Gorman">Don Gorman</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>—166</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Jacob_Hornberger" title="Jacob Hornberger" class="mw-redirect">Jacob Hornberger</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>—120</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Barry_Hess" title="Barry Hess" class="mw-redirect">Barry Hess</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> 53</li> <li>None of the Above—23</li> <li>other write-ins—15</li> <li>David Hollist of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>—8</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Libertarian_Party" title="United States Libertarian Party" class="mw-redirect">Libertarian Party's</a> National Nominating Convention nominated <a href="/wiki/Harry_Browne" title="Harry Browne">Harry Browne</a> of Tennessee and <a href="/wiki/Art_Olivier" title="Art Olivier">Art Olivier</a> of California for Vice President. Browne was nominated on the first ballot and Olivier received the Vice Presidential nomination on the second ballot.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Browne appeared on every state ballot except for Arizona, due to a minor dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_of_Arizona" title="Libertarian Party of Arizona">Libertarian Party of Arizona</a> (who instead nominated <a href="/wiki/L._Neil_Smith" title="L. Neil Smith">L. Neil Smith</a>) and the national <a href="/wiki/United_States_Libertarian_Party" title="United States Libertarian Party" class="mw-redirect">Libertarian Party</a>.</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution_Party_nomination">Constitution Party nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Constitution Party nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Constitution_Party_(United_States)" title="Constitution Party (United States)">Constitution Party</a> candidates <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Howard_Phillips_(politics)" title="Howard Phillips (politics)" class="mw-redirect">Howard Phillips</a></li> <li><a href="/wiki/Herb_Titus" title="Herb Titus" class="mw-redirect">Herb Titus</a></li> <li>Mathew Zupan</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p>The Constitution Party nominated <a href="/wiki/Howard_Phillips_(politics)" title="Howard Phillips (politics)" class="mw-redirect">Howard Phillips</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> for a third time and <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Frazier" title="Curtis Frazier">Curtis Frazier</a> of <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>. The Constitution Party was on the ballot in 41 states.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_Law_Party_nomination">Natural Law Party nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Natural Law Party nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/John_Hagelin" title="John Hagelin">John Hagelin</a> of Iowa and <a href="/wiki/Nat_Goldhaber" title="Nat Goldhaber">Nat Goldhaber</a> of California</li> </ul> <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Natural_Law_Party" title="United States Natural Law Party" class="mw-redirect">Natural Law Party</a> held its national convention in <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" title="Arlington, Virginia" class="mw-redirect">Arlington, Virginia</a>, August 31 – September 2, nominating a ticket of Hagelin/Goldhaber via unanimous decision without a roll-call vote.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The party was on 38 of the 51 ballots nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_election_campaign">General election campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: General election campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <p>Although the campaign focused mainly on domestic issues, such as the projected budget surplus, proposed reforms of <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)" title="Medicare (United States)">Medicare</a>, health care, and competing plans for tax relief, foreign policy was often an issue. Bush criticized <a href="/wiki/Clinton_administration" title="Clinton administration" class="mw-redirect">Clinton administration</a> policies in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, where 18 Americans died in 1993 trying to sort out warring factions, and in the Balkans, where United States peacekeeping troops perform a variety of functions. "I don't think our troops ought to be used for what's called <a href="/wiki/Nation-building" title="Nation-building">nation-building</a>," Bush said in the second <a href="/wiki/American_presidential_debate" title="American presidential debate" class="mw-redirect">presidential debate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Bush also pledged to bridge partisan gaps in the nation's capital, claiming the atmosphere in Washington stood in the way of progress on necessary reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Gore, meanwhile, questioned Bush's fitness for the job, pointing to gaffes made by Bush in interviews and speeches and suggesting the Texas governor lacked the necessary experience to be president.</p> <p><a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Impeachment of Bill Clinton">impeachment</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lewinsky_scandal" title="Lewinsky scandal">sex scandal</a> that led up to it cast a shadow on the campaign, particularly on his vice president's run to replace him. Republicans strongly denounced the Clinton scandals, particularly Bush, who made his repeated promise to restore "honor and dignity" to the White House a centerpiece of his campaign. Gore studiously avoided the Clinton scandals, as did Lieberman, even though Lieberman had been the first Democratic senator to denounce Clinton's misbehavior. In fact, some media observers theorized that Gore actually chose Lieberman in an attempt to separate himself from Clinton's past misdeeds, and help blunt the GOP's attempts to link him to his boss.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Others pointed to the passionate kiss Gore gave his wife during the <a href="/wiki/2000_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2000 Democratic National Convention">Democratic Convention</a>, as a signal that despite the allegations against Clinton, Gore himself was a faithful husband.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Gore avoided appearing with Clinton, who was shunted to low visibility appearances in areas where he was popular. Experts have argued that this cost Gore votes from some of Clinton's core supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p><a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">Ralph Nader</a> was the most successful of third-party candidates, drawing 2.74 percent of the popular vote. His campaign was marked by a traveling tour of large "super-rallies" held in sports arenas like <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>, with retired <a href="/wiki/Talk_show_host" title="Talk show host" class="mw-redirect">talk show host</a> <a href="/wiki/Phil_Donahue" title="Phil Donahue">Phil Donahue</a> as master of ceremonies. After initially ignoring Nader, the Gore campaign made a pitch to (potential) Nader supporters in the final weeks of the campaign, downplaying Gore's differences with Nader on the issues and arguing that Gore's ideas were more similar to Nader's than Bush's were, and noting that Gore had a better chance of winning than Nader. On the other side, the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Leadership_Council" title="Republican Leadership Council">Republican Leadership Council</a> ran pro-Nader ads in a few states in an effort to split the liberal vote.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> In the aftermath of the campaign, many Gore supporters claimed that Nader acted as a <a href="/wiki/Spoiler_effect" title="Spoiler effect">spoiler</a> in the election, that Nader votes would have been cast for Gore, and that Nader threw the election outcome to Bush. Nader dismissed such concerns, claiming his objective in the campaign was to pass the 5-percent threshold so his Green Party would be eligible for matching funds in future races.</p> <p>Both vice presidential candidates <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Lieberman" title="Joe Lieberman">Joe Lieberman</a> campaigned aggressively in the 2000 presidential election. Both camps made numerous campaign stops nationwide, often just missing each other such as when Cheney, <a href="/wiki/Hadassah_Lieberman" title="Hadassah Lieberman">Hadassah Lieberman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tipper_Gore" title="Tipper Gore">Tipper Gore</a> attended Chicago's <a href="/wiki/Taste_of_Polonia" title="Taste of Polonia">Taste of Polonia</a> over <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_Weekend" title="Labor Day Weekend" class="mw-redirect">Labor Day Weekend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidential_debates">Presidential debates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Presidential debates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_debates,_2000" title="United States presidential election debates, 2000">United States presidential election debates, 2000</a></div> <p>There were three presidential debates:</p> <ul> <li>October 3, 2000, at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts" title="University of Massachusetts">University of Massachusetts</a> in Boston<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></li> <li>October 11, 2000, at <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_University" title="Wake Forest University">Wake Forest University</a> in Winston-Salem, North Carolina<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></li> <li>October 17, 2000, at <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_in_Saint_Louis" title="Washington University in Saint Louis" class="mw-redirect">Washington University in Saint Louis</a>, Missouri<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></li> </ul> <p>There was also one vice-presidential debate:</p> <ul> <li>October 5, 2000, at <a href="/wiki/Centre_College" title="Centre College">Centre College</a> in Kentucky<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></li> </ul> <p>The <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Presidential_Debates" title="Commission on Presidential Debates">Commission on Presidential Debates</a>, formed by Democratic and Republican party leaders, set rules that effectively excluded all but the two major party candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Ralph Nader was blocked from attending a closed circuit screening of the first debate in spite of his holding a ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> He was barred from attending an interview near the site of the third debate in spite of having a "perimeter pass".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Nader later sued the CPD for its role in the former incident. A settlement was reached that included an apology to Nader.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_expressions_and_phrases">Notable expressions and phrases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notable expressions and phrases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <ul> <li><a href="/wiki/Lockbox" title="Lockbox" class="mw-redirect">Lockbox</a>/Rainy Day fund: Gore's description of what he would do with the federal budget surplus.</li> <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Gore_and_information_technology#1999_CNN_interview" title="Al Gore and information technology">Al Gore invented the Internet</a>: an interpretation of a quote by Al Gore in which he said that he "took the initiative in creating the Internet", to say that he was on the committee that funded the research which led to the formation of the Internet.</li> </ul> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results">Results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="thumb tright"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg/200px-Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg" width="200" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg/300px-Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg/400px-Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="594" /></a> <div class="thumbcaption"> <div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pbc-fl-2000-recount-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div> Palm Beach County recount</div> </div> </div> <p>With the exceptions of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and Gore's home state of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, Bush carried the Southern states by comfortable margins (including then-President Bill Clinton's home state of Arkansas) and also secured wins in <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, most of the rural <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern</a> farming states, most of the Rocky Mountain states, and Alaska. Gore balanced Bush by sweeping the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeastern United States</a> (with the sole exception of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, which Bush won narrowly), most of the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Midwest" title="Upper Midwest">Upper Midwest</a>, and all of the Pacific Coast states of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(U.S._state)" title="Washington (U.S. state)" class="mw-redirect">Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, and carried <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, as well.</p> <p>As the night wore on, the returns in a handful of small-to-medium sized states, including <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>, were extremely close; however it was the state of Florida that would make clear the winner of the election. As the final national results were tallied the following morning, Bush had clearly won a total of 246 electoral votes, while Gore had won 255 votes. 270 votes were needed to win. Two smaller states—<a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> (5 electoral votes) and Oregon (7 electoral votes)—were still too close to call. It was Florida (25 electoral votes), however, that the <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">news media</a> focused their attention on. Mathematically, Florida's 25 electoral votes became the key to an election win for either candidate. Although both New Mexico and Oregon were declared in favor of Gore over the next few days, Florida's statewide vote took center stage because that state's winner would ultimately win the election. The outcome of the election was not known for more than a month after the balloting ended because of the extended process of counting and then recounting Florida's presidential ballots.</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_recount">Florida recount</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Florida recount">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Florida,_2000" title="United States presidential election in Florida, 2000">United States presidential election in Florida, 2000</a></div> <div class="thumb tleft"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg/170px-TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg/255px-TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg/340px-TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1750" data-file-height="2571" /></a> <div class="thumbcaption"> <div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TallahaseePalmBeachBallotBox1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div> 2000 Palm Beach County voting stand and ballot box</div> </div> </div> <p>Between 7:50 p.m. and 8:00 p.m. EST on election day, just as the polls closed in the largely Republican Florida panhandle, which is in the Central time zone, all major television news networks (CNN, NBC, FOX, CBS, MSNBC, and ABC) declared that Gore had carried Florida's 25 electoral votes. They based this prediction substantially on <a href="/wiki/Exit_poll" title="Exit poll">exit polls</a>. However, in the actual vote tally Bush began to take a wide lead early in Florida, and by 10 p.m. EST the networks had retracted that prediction and placed Florida back into the "undecided" column. At approximately 2:30 a.m., with some 85% of the votes counted in Florida and Bush leading Gore by more than 100,000 votes, the networks declared that Bush had carried Florida and therefore had been elected President. However, most of the remaining votes to be counted in Florida were located in three heavily Democratic counties—<a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County" title="Miami-Dade County" class="mw-redirect">Miami-Dade</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County" title="Palm Beach County" class="mw-redirect">Palm Beach</a>—and as their votes were reported Gore began to gain on Bush. By 4:30 a.m., after all votes were counted, Gore had narrowed Bush's margin to just over 2,000 votes, and the networks retracted their predictions that Bush had won Florida and the presidency. Gore, who had privately conceded the election to Bush, withdrew his concession. The final result in Florida was slim enough to require a mandatory recount (by machine) under state law; Bush's lead had dwindled to about 300 votes by the time it was completed later that week. A count of overseas military ballots later boosted his margin to about 900 votes.</p> <div class="thumb tright"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG/220px-FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG/330px-FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG/440px-FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2755" data-file-height="1528" /></a> <div class="thumbcaption"> <div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FlaSupremeCrtBldgFeb08.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div> Florida Supreme Court</div> </div> </div> <p>Most of the post-electoral controversy revolved around Gore's request for hand recounts in four counties (Broward, Miami Dade, Palm Beach, and <a href="/wiki/Volusia_County,_Florida" title="Volusia County, Florida">Volusia</a>), as provided under Florida state law. <a href="/wiki/Florida_Secretary_of_State" title="Florida Secretary of State" class="mw-redirect">Florida Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Harris" title="Katherine Harris">Katherine Harris</a> announced she would reject any revised totals from those counties if they were not turned in by November 14, the statutory deadline for amended returns. The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Supreme_Court" title="Florida Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">Florida Supreme Court</a> extended the deadline to November 26, a decision later <a href="/wiki/Vacated" title="Vacated" class="mw-redirect">vacated</a> by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court" title="U.S. Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Supreme Court</a>. Miami-Dade eventually halted its recount and resubmitted its original total to the state canvassing board, while Palm Beach County failed to meet the extended deadline. On November 26, the state canvassing board certified Bush the winner of Florida's electors by 537 votes. Gore formally contested the certified results, but a state court decision overruling Gore was reversed by the Florida Supreme Court, which ordered a recount of over 70,000 ballots previously rejected by machine counters. The U.S. Supreme Court quickly halted that order the next day with the concurring opinion that a recount of votes "of questionable legality does [...] threaten irreparable harm" to Bush as "each manual recount produces a degradation of the ballots."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>On December 12, the Supreme Court <a href="/wiki/Bush_v._Gore" title="Bush v. Gore">ruled</a> in a 7–2 vote that the Florida Supreme Court's ruling requiring a statewide recount of ballots was unconstitutional, and in a 5–4 vote that the Florida recounts could not be completed before a December 12 "safe harbor" deadline, and should therefore cease and the previously certified total should hold.</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_results">National results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: National results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <p>Though Gore came in second in the electoral vote, he received 543,895 more popular votes than Bush.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2000_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2000-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Gore failed to win the popular vote in his home state, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, which both he and his father had represented in the Senate, making him the first major-party presidential candidate to have lost his home state since <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">George McGovern</a> lost <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1972" title="United States presidential election, 1972">1972</a>. Bush lost in <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, the state of his birth. Bush is also the first Republican in American history to win the presidency without winning Vermont or Illinois, the second Republican to win the presidency without winning California (<a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">James A. Garfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_1880" title="U.S. presidential election, 1880" class="mw-redirect">1880</a> was the first), and the only winning Republican not to receive any electoral votes from California (Garfield received one vote in 1880).</p> <table class="wikitable"> <tr> <th rowspan="2">Presidential candidate</th> <th rowspan="2">Party</th> <th rowspan="2">Home state</th> <th colspan="2">Popular vote</th> <th rowspan="2">Electoral<br /> vote</th> <th colspan="3">Running mate</th> </tr> <tr> <th>Count</th> <th>Pct</th> <th>Vice-presidential candidate</th> <th>Home state</th> <th>Elect. vote</th> </tr> <tr> <td><b><a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Maine and Nebraska district results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> <p><sup>★</sup>Maine and Nebraska each allow for their electoral votes to be split between candidates. In both states, two electoral votes are awarded to the winner of the statewide race and one electoral vote is awarded to the winner of each congressional district. <td>Reform</td> <td>49</td> <td>448,895</td> </tr> <tr style="background:#FFFF66"> <td>Browne / Olivier</td> <td>Libertarian</td> <td>49+DC</td> <td>384,431</td> </tr> <tr style="background:#d8a6ff"> <td>Phillips / Frazier</td> <td>Constitution</td> <td>41</td> <td>98,020</td> </tr> <tr> <td>Hagelin / Goldhaber</td> <td>Natural Law</td> <td>38</td> <td>83,714</td> </tr> </table> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <p>After Florida was decided and Gore conceded, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Texas Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> became the <a href="/wiki/President-elect_of_the_United_States" title="President-elect of the United States">President-elect</a> and began forming his <a href="/wiki/Presidential_transition" title="Presidential transition" class="mw-redirect">transition committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In a speech on December 13, in the Texas House of Representatives chamber,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Bush stated he was reaching across party lines to bridge a divided America, saying, "the President of the United States is the President of every single American, of every race, and every background."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_recount">Post recount</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Post recount">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <p>On January 6, 2001, a <a href="/wiki/Joint_session_of_the_United_States_Congress" title="Joint session of the United States Congress">joint session of Congress</a> met to certify the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral vote</a>. Twenty members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>, most of them Democratic members of the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Black_Caucus" title="Congressional Black Caucus">Congressional Black Caucus</a>, rose one-by-one to file objections to the electoral votes of Florida. However, according to an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_States)" title="Electoral Commission (United States)">1877</a> law, any such objection had to be sponsored by both a representative and a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">senator</a>. No senator would co-sponsor these objections, deferring to the Supreme Court's ruling. Therefore, Gore, who presided in his capacity as <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">President of the Senate</a>, ruled each of these objections out of order.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>Subsequently, the joint session of Congress certified the electoral votes from all 50 states and the District of Columbia. Bush took the oath of office on January 20, 2001. He would serve for the next eight years. Gore declined to run for president in 2004 and 2008.</p> <p>The first independent recount was conducted by the <i>Miami Herald</i> and <i>USA Today</i>. The commission found that under most recount scenarios, Bush would have won the election, but Gore would have won using the most generous standards.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>Ultimately, a media consortium—comprising the <i>New York Times</i>, <i>Washington Post</i>, <i>Wall Street Journal</i>, Tribune Co. (parent of the <i>Los Angeles Times</i>), Associated Press, CNN, <i>Palm Beach Post</i> and <i>St. Petersburg Times</i><sup id="cite_ref-fair2002_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fair2002-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>—hired the <a href="/wiki/National_Opinion_Research_Center" title="National Opinion Research Center" class="mw-redirect">National Opinion Research Center</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> to examine 175,010 ballots that were collected from the entire state, not just the disputed counties that were discounted; these ballots contained undervotes (votes with no choice made for president) and overvotes (votes made with more than one choice marked). Their goal was to determine the reliability and accuracy of the systems used for the voting process. The NORC concluded that if the disputes over the validity of all the ballots statewide in question had been consistently resolved and <i>any</i> uniform standard applied, the electoral result would have been reversed and Gore would have won by 107–115 votes if only two of the three coders had to agree on the ballot. When counting ballots wherein all three coders agreed, Gore would have won the most restrictive scenario by 127 votes and Bush would have won the most inclusive scenario by 110 votes. Inclusive in media reporting likely refers to including the undervotes (only) as these people were then included in the vote. Whether overvotes were truly nullified in counts is not known.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>Subsequent analyses cast further doubt on conclusions that Bush likely would have won anyway, had the U.S. Supreme Court not intervened. An analysis of the NORC data by <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> researcher Steven F. Freeman and journalist <a href="/wiki/Joel_Bleifuss" title="Joel Bleifuss">Joel Bleifuss</a> concluded that a recount of all uncounted votes using any standard (inclusive, strict, statewide or county by county), Gore would have been the victor.<sup id="cite_ref-freemanbleifuss_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freemanbleifuss-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Such a statewide review including all uncounted votes was a very real possibility, as Leon County Circuit Court Judge <a href="/wiki/Terry_Lewis_(Florida_judge)" title="Terry Lewis (Florida judge)">Terry Lewis</a>, whom the Florida Supreme Court had assigned to oversee the statewide recount, had scheduled a hearing for December 13 (mooted by the U.S. Supreme Court's final ruling on the 12th) to consider the question of including overvotes as well as undervotes, and subsequent statements by Judge Lewis and internal court documents support the likelihood of including overvotes in the recount.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek2001_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek2001-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a> professor of public policy Lance deHaven-Smith observed that, even considering only undervotes, "under any of the five most reasonable interpretations of the Florida Supreme Court ruling, Gore does, in fact, more than make up the deficit".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fairness_and_Accuracy_in_Reporting" title="Fairness and Accuracy in Reporting">Fairness and Accuracy in Reporting</a>'s analysis of the NORC study and media coverage of it supports these interpretations and criticizes the coverage of the study by media outlets such as the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a></i> and the other media consortium members.<sup id="cite_ref-fair2002_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fair2002-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voting_machines">Voting machines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Voting machines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <p>Because the 2000 presidential election was so close in Florida, the United States government and state governments pushed for <a href="/wiki/Election_reform" title="Election reform" class="mw-redirect">election reform</a> to be prepared by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2004" title="United States presidential election, 2004">2004 presidential election</a>. Many of Florida's year 2000 election night problems stemmed from <a href="/wiki/Usability" title="Usability">usability</a> and ballot design factors with voting systems, including the potentially confusing "<a href="/wiki/Butterfly_ballot" title="Butterfly ballot" class="mw-redirect">butterfly ballot</a>". Many voters had difficulties with the paper-based <a href="/wiki/Voting_machine#Punch_card" title="Voting machine">punch card</a> voting machines and were either unable to understand the required process for voting or unable to perform the process. This resulted in an unusual amount of <a href="/wiki/Overvote" title="Overvote">overvote</a> (voting for more candidates than is allowed) and <a href="/wiki/Undervote" title="Undervote">undervotes</a> (voting for fewer than the minimum candidates, including none at all). Many undervotes were potentially caused by either voter error or errors with the punch card paper ballots resulting in hanging, dimpled, or pregnant <a href="/wiki/Chad_(paper)" title="Chad (paper)">chad</a>.</p> <p>A proposed solution to these problems was the installation of modern <a href="/wiki/Electronic_voting" title="Electronic voting">electronic voting</a> machines. The United States Presidential Election of 2000 spurred the debate about election and voting reform, but it did not end it.</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exit_polling_and_declaration_of_vote_winners">Exit polling and declaration of vote winners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Exit polling and declaration of vote winners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <p>The <a href="/wiki/Voter_News_Service" title="Voter News Service">Voter News Service</a>'s reputation was damaged by its treatment of Florida's presidential vote in 2000. Breaking its own guidelines, VNS called the state as a win for Gore 12 minutes before polls closed in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">Florida panhandle</a>. Although most of the state is in the Eastern Time Zone, counties in the Florida panhandle, located in the Central Time Zone, had not yet closed their polls. More seriously, inconsistent polling results caused the VNS to change its call twice, first from Gore to Bush, and then to "too close to call".</p> <p>Also, charges of media bias were levied against the networks by Republicans. They claimed that the networks called states more quickly for Al Gore than for George W. Bush. Congress held hearings on this matter and the networks claimed to have no intentional bias in their election night reporting. However, a study of the calls made on election night 2000 indicated that states carried by Gore were called more quickly than states won by Bush; however, notable Bush states, like New Hampshire and Florida, were very close, and close Gore states like Iowa, Oregon, New Mexico and Wisconsin were called late as well.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="More_consequences">More consequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: More consequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <p>In the aftermath of the election, the <a href="/wiki/Help_America_Vote_Act" title="Help America Vote Act">Help America Vote Act</a> (HAVA) was passed to help states upgrade their election technology in the hopes of preventing similar problems in future elections. Unfortunately, the electronic voting systems that many states purchased to comply with HAVA actually caused problems in the presidential election of 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>Many Democrats blame third party candidate <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">Ralph Nader</a>, claiming he <a href="/wiki/Vote_splitting" title="Vote splitting">split votes</a> with Gore. Nader received 97,000 votes in Florida (for comparison, there were 111,251 <a href="/wiki/Overvotes" title="Overvotes" class="mw-redirect">overvotes</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, Nader received 22,000 votes in New Hampshire, where Bush beat Gore by 7,000 votes. Either state would have won the election for Gore. Defenders of Nader, including <a href="/wiki/Tom_Tomorrow" title="Tom Tomorrow">Dan Perkins</a>, argued that the margin in Florida was small enough that Democrats could blame any number of third-party candidates for the defeat, including <a href="/wiki/Workers_World_Party" title="Workers World Party">Workers World Party</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Monica_Moorehead" title="Monica Moorehead">Monica Moorehead</a>, who received 1,500 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> But the controversy with Nader also drained energy from the Democratic party as divisive debate went on in the months leading up to the election. Nader's reputation was hurt by this perception, and may have hindered his goals as an activist. For example, <i><a href="/wiki/Mother_Jones_(magazine)" title="Mother Jones (magazine)">Mother Jones</a></i> wrote, "For evidence of how rank-and-file liberals have turned against Nader, one need look no further than the empire he created. <a href="/wiki/Public_Citizen" title="Public Citizen">Public Citizen</a>, the organization (Nader) founded in 1971, has a new fundraising problem—its founder. After the election, contributions dropped... When people inquire about Nader's relationship to the organization, Public Citizen sends out a letter that begins with a startling new disclaimer: 'Although Ralph Nader was our founder, he has not held an official position in the organization since 1980 and does not serve on the board. Public Citizen—and the other groups that Mr. Nader founded—act independently.'"<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>Democratic party strategist and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Leadership_Council" title="Democratic Leadership Council">Democratic Leadership Council</a> (DLC) chair <a href="/wiki/Al_From" title="Al From">Al From</a> expressed a different view. In the January 24, 2001, issue<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> of the DLC's <i>Blueprint</i> magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> he wrote, "I think they're wrong on all counts. The assertion that Nader's marginal vote hurt Gore is not borne out by polling data. When exit pollers asked voters how they would have voted in a two-way race, Bush actually won by a point. That was better than he did with Nader in the race."</p> <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press_influence_on_race">Press influence on race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Press influence on race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> <p>In their 2007 book <i>The Nightly News Nightmare: Network Television's Coverage of US Presidential Elections, 1988-2004,</i> professors Stephen J. Farnsworth and S. Robert Lichter alleged most media outlets influenced the outcome of the election through the use of <a href="/wiki/Horse_race_journalism" title="Horse race journalism">horse race journalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Peter Hart and Jim Naureckas, two commentators for <a href="/wiki/Fairness_and_Accuracy_in_Reporting" title="Fairness and Accuracy in Reporting">Fairness and Accuracy in Reporting</a> (FAIR), called the media "serial exaggerators" and noted how several media outlets were constantly exaggerating criticism of Gore,<sup id="cite_ref-ipqvzww_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipqvzww-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> like falsely claiming that Gore lied when he claimed he spoke in an overcrowded science class in Sarasota, Florida,<sup id="cite_ref-ipqvzww_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipqvzww-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> and giving Bush a pass on certain issues, such as the fact that Bush wildly exaggerated how much money he signed into the annual Texas state budget to help the uninsured during his second debate with Gore in October 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-ipqvzww_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipqvzww-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In the April 2000 issue of <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a>, columnist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Parry_(journalist)" title="Robert Parry (journalist)">Robert Parry</a> also noted how several media outlets exaggerated Gore's supposed claim that he "discovered" the <a href="/wiki/Love_Canal" title="Love Canal">Love Canal</a> neighborhood in <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_New_York" title="Niagara Falls, New York">Niagara Falls, New York</a> during a campaign speech in Concord, New Hampshire on November 30, 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-kqvz_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kqvz-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> when he had only claimed he "found" it after it was already evacuated in 1978 because of chemical contamination.<sup id="cite_ref-kqvz_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kqvz-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a> columnist Eric Boehlert also argued that media outlets exaggerated criticism of Gore as early as July 22, 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-ipqkva_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipqkva-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> when Gore, known for being an environmentalist, had a friend release 500 million gallons of water into a drought stricken river to help keep his boat afloat for a photo shoot;<sup id="cite_ref-ipqkva_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipqkva-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> media outlets, however, exaggerated the actual number of gallons that were released and claimed it was 4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-ipqkva_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipqkva-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span Bush">First inauguration of George W. Bush</a></li> </ul> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_presidential_election,_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> <ol class="references"> <li id="cite_note-turnout-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-turnout_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://elections.gmu.edu/Turnout_2000G.html">"2000 General Election Turnout Rates"</a>. <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_University" title="George Mason University">George Mason University</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.
